    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6181027440535638257">Brigitte is an emissary of nature chosen to renew the treaty between Atlantis and the ancient bloodline of Lemuria. Her sacred betrothal would renew the elemental function of the Crystal Grid that powers the ten kingdoms of Atlantis. But her people are attacked by a storm of shadows, and now she is running for her life. <br/><br/>Upon her arrival in the ruling city, she meets D’Vini</span>
  <span id="freeText6181027440535638257" style="display:none">Brigitte is an emissary of nature chosen to renew the treaty between Atlantis and the ancient bloodline of Lemuria. Her sacred betrothal would renew the elemental function of the Crystal Grid that powers the ten kingdoms of Atlantis. But her people are attacked by a storm of shadows, and now she is running for her life. <br /><br />Upon her arrival in the ruling city, she meets D’Vinid, a dejected musician who lives the quintessential Atlantean lifestyle of revelry, escapism and apathy. Under the eclipse of a holy festival, they are swept into an attraction they cannot resist. Their union may protect humanity from its worst enemy - the shadows of Atlantis. But there is one problem, this man is not her betrothed. <br /><br />Brigitte discovers the Grid is corrupted by psychic parasites that feed off human suffering, an epidemic called “the madness”. The rituals required to charge the Grid with psychic emanations have been poorly attended, and this has caused the Grid to malfunction. But as nature always strives toward balance, the crystals have activated a genetic upgrade among the people. The youth have begun to express supernatural powers. Could it be that D’Vinid and Brigitte are meant to be leaders among the awakened? And if so, why does it seem impossible for them to be together? <br /><br />A mysterious tale of romance, seduction and betrayal that reaches just enough into the modern mind to ask - will we learn the lessons of Atlantis?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6181027440535638257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1716289164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716289164" />
    <a title="Melissa Souza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40579850-melissa-souza"><img alt="Melissa Souza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525391354p2/40579850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716289164?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Souza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Souza" href="/user/show/40579850-melissa-souza">Melissa Souza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27428436-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716289164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15008754945861331784">** (I received a free copy of this book from the author in exchange for an honest review).<br/><br/>** Aspects of the plot have been revealed in this review.<br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The described Atlantis in this book is definitely not the one you hear of in other stories. Mara Powers has brilliantly managed to weave an intricate world around this mythical city but it is filled with gadgets and a magic system that goes beyond one's scope of imagination. The worldbuliding is highly intricate with detailed descriptions of </span>
  <span id="freeText15008754945861331784" style="display:none">** (I received a free copy of this book from the author in exchange for an honest review).<br /><br />** Aspects of the plot have been revealed in this review.<br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />The described Atlantis in this book is definitely not the one you hear of in other stories. Mara Powers has brilliantly managed to weave an intricate world around this mythical city but it is filled with gadgets and a magic system that goes beyond one's scope of imagination. The worldbuliding is highly intricate with detailed descriptions of fashion, political divisions, temple sects, rituals, traditions and so on. I was really pleased that a glossary was given at the end of the story because many of the terms were highly confusing and this helped clarify their meanings.<br /><br />Out of all the characters, D'Vinid was the most rounded. I really liked how his character progressed throughout the novel. However, Brigitte was described in a rather cliched way and I just couldn't connect with her character. The romance between them also felt too contrived and sudden. We don't get a gradual build up. I would have liked to see a forbidden romance blossoming between them. The other minor characters played their roles well in the story. Kyliron has definitely got me intrigued. I am unsure of what his whole role is but I feel he is connected to the darkness somehow. I would love to know about him. My favorite part in the whole novel would have to be the part about the darkness. This definitely gave a book a touch of mystery and gave the reader relief from the otherwise heavy content of the novel. However, I do feel that the way the madness begins wasn't fully described. Maybe because this ended up being relegated to a side story in the novel and the focus was more on the Queen Impending and D'Vinid.<br /><br />My only negative about this book was that the reading felt a little tedious at times. I appreciate Mara's extensive research into this novel. It definitely led to a rich backdrop for the story. But while reading, I constantly felt that there needed to be some lighter elements in the book. For example, when Lukias and Brigitte have their conversations, you don't connect with their relationship as brother and sister. Mostly they speak about the Atlantean customs and the magic system which I found to be more info dumping and disconcerting. I would say, in hindsight, I would have liked to see the characters engaging with others in a way that brought out their emotions and personality more. This would have taken the novel to a whole new level.<br /><br />Besides that small criticism, I did enjoy the story at the end of the day. It was a highly immersive read which fantasy readers would love. The book does end of a major cliffhanger and I hope to get to read the sequel soon because I look forward to the journey ahead for the characters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15008754945861331784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3593047393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3593047393" />
    <a title="Lucie V." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v"><img alt="Lucie V." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597788485p2/84801697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3593047393?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucie V." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucie V." href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v">Lucie V.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42967364-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3593047393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7206053076417496314">I received a copy of this book via NetGalley.<br/><br/>2.5 stars<br/><br/>The description of Atlantis in this book is very original and not what we are used to. There is a mix of technology and ancient history. The fashion and way of living of the inhabitants of Atlantis are well described and interesting. We can feel the extensive research that was done by the author, it is an impressive work, but some details were confusing at first, and honestly, I mixed up a few characters also during the first chapters. There </span>
  <span id="freeText7206053076417496314" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book via NetGalley.<br /><br />2.5 stars<br /><br />The description of Atlantis in this book is very original and not what we are used to. There is a mix of technology and ancient history. The fashion and way of living of the inhabitants of Atlantis are well described and interesting. We can feel the extensive research that was done by the author, it is an impressive work, but some details were confusing at first, and honestly, I mixed up a few characters also during the first chapters. There is a glossary at the end of the book, but with the kindle version, it was harder to go back and forth to the glossary every time there was a new word, so it was confusing and I had trouble understanding a few concepts because they were not clearly explained in the story. <br /><br />The characters were okay. Brigitte was a little cliché at times honestly and I didn’t like her that much. D’Vinid is more interesting, he also has a nicer evolution throughout the book. The romance between him and Brigitte is awful though. I understand why it happens, but it is so sudden! There is no build-up, I am not even sure that he knew her name the first time they kissed. It is insta-lust and insta-love (and insta-weird) and it was intense, but not in a good way.<br /><br />Overall, the plot is good, but some parts were distracting. There is also a lot of vocabulary to get used to at the beginning, so it was confusing even with the glossary. There is mystery and I liked the idea of the darkness invading people and feeding on their negative emotions. Still, I was not compelled to continue reading this story. I finished it because it was interesting enough, but I had to force myself to read a little bit of it everyday, else it would have taken me twice as much time to read it. It did not live up to my expectations, but it is not a bad book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7206053076417496314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433921806" />
    <a title="Mara Powers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41710347-mara-powers"><img alt="Mara Powers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602285600p2/41710347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433921806?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara Powers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara Powers" href="/user/show/41710347-mara-powers">Mara Powers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433921806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16834800584199540596">From Readers' Favorite!!!<br/><br/>Review Rating: <br/>5 stars! <br/>Reviewed By Tracy Slowiak for Readers’ Favorite<br/><br/>In a brand new novel by debut author Mara Powers, Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening, readers will be taken along on an absolutely epic journey to amazing Atlantis, focus of stories both old and new. The Atlantis of author Powers’ work is a beautiful paradise, one in which everyone can live to their highest potential, and in complete peace with nature. Atlantis is run by the Crystal Grid, energized by the</span>
  <span id="freeText16834800584199540596" style="display:none">From Readers' Favorite!!!<br /><br />Review Rating: <br />5 stars! <br />Reviewed By Tracy Slowiak for Readers’ Favorite<br /><br />In a brand new novel by debut author Mara Powers, Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening, readers will be taken along on an absolutely epic journey to amazing Atlantis, focus of stories both old and new. The Atlantis of author Powers’ work is a beautiful paradise, one in which everyone can live to their highest potential, and in complete peace with nature. Atlantis is run by the Crystal Grid, energized by the psychic power of its inhabitants, and this has worked well for thousands of years. But now the grid is in danger. Parasites feeding off of humans’ negative emotions are pulling energy away from the grid. Atlantis and all of its perfection could be lost forever. D’Vinid, a musician who feels rather rejected and can think of nothing but his personal problems, meets Brigitte from Atlantis, and finds that he may be the only key to the survival of this idyllic place. But can someone so flawed, so enmeshed in his own private problems, really be able to move forward to help a society in desperate need? You’ll need to read the book to find out!<br /><br /> I loved this book. Loved. It. Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening is an absolutely fantastic read that had me turning the pages obsessively from the very beginning. Once I started this book, I simply could not put it down, it was that good. Author Mara Powers has done a fabulous job in creating characters that her readers will truly care about and connect with. Her ability to create a fantastic but believable world is simply second to none. Any reader who loves a great read in the fantasy genre, or simply a wonderful work of fiction, should absolutely read Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening. I highly recommend this book, and look forward to reading more in this promising new series and from the highly talented newcomer, Mara Powers, hopefully in the very near future! <br /></span>

<div id="review_2690031885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2690031885" />
    <a title="Ellie Mitchell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52372064-ellie-mitchell"><img alt="Ellie Mitchell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589830738p2/52372064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2690031885?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellie Mitchell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie Mitchell" href="/user/show/52372064-ellie-mitchell">Ellie Mitchell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2690031885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2911515969085344371">Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening is a fictional novel that explores the culture and downfall of the legendary lost city of Atlantis. Mara Powers has studied this legendary place for over thirty years and has created a compelling story of humanity’s inner spirit, our relationship with nature, and the greed/deceptive employed by those in government.<br/><br/><br/>The story follows Brigitte (would-be Queen of Atlantis and daughter of a powerful Dreamseer clan) and D’vinid (a disgraced royal and famed musician, dubb</span>
  <span id="freeText2911515969085344371" style="display:none">Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening is a fictional novel that explores the culture and downfall of the legendary lost city of Atlantis. Mara Powers has studied this legendary place for over thirty years and has created a compelling story of humanity’s inner spirit, our relationship with nature, and the greed/deceptive employed by those in government.<br /><br /><br />The story follows Brigitte (would-be Queen of Atlantis and daughter of a powerful Dreamseer clan) and D’vinid (a disgraced royal and famed musician, dubbed: The Prophet-Singer.) From the start of the book, it is clear that they are destined to play a big role in each other's lives. Both are linked in some way to the current king of Atlantis, Kyrilon, a corrupt puppet of evil spiritual forces.<br /><br />One thing I found particularly fascinating was the concept of ‘The Grid,’ the main power source of Atlantis, made up of channelled human consciousness (AI mind hub, anyone?) Alas, the Grid has been corrupted by a secret society, hell-bent on destroying all that would see humans flourish naturally.<br /><br /><br />Also refreshing was Power’s vivid world descriptions, detailing everyday life in Atlantis. The desires and fears of citizens are well explored, painting a realistic picture of an ancient civilisation on the brink of its downfall. By far my favourite parts of this novel are the parallels drawn between the crumbling culture of Atlantis and our modern day world.<br /><br />*Listed below are some of my favourite quotes that display these comparisons.*<br /><br /><br />‘Dark times had fallen over Atlantis. Everything felt wrong...the feeling was beginning to seem more widespread.’<br /><br />In modern times, our societies seem to be collapsing, with everyone sealing themselves off in their unique groups and sharing the exact same thought process, becoming more manic and refusing to even discuss separate opinions and ideas from our own.<br /><br /><br />(About the Atlanteans:) ‘...not a soul took interest in their passing- they did not have the awareness of the dream-clans. They were much more self-absorbed.’<br /><br />In our modern world, a lot of us are constantly in competition with others for status in things such as beauty or intelligence, so much so that we become self-absorbed, stuck in our little bubbles. Modern society is increasingly obsessed with vanity and the concept of self, above natural human traits such as trust, love, loyalty, and true individualisation, outside of collective groups.<br /><br /><br />‘Revelries were a cultural mainstay all through Atlantean history. They thought it to be their birthright as humans to enjoy the pleasures of sensory perception while reaching for the bliss of higher consciousness.’<br /><br />For me, this was the quote that hit the nail on the head and made the most profound comparison. More and more people want to simply enjoy the pleasures and profits of life without actually putting in the work for such things. We are increasingly seeing it as our divine right to be pleased and to have instant gratification, perhaps seeking some higher power but rejecting it when the effort seems too great.<br /><br /><br />…….<br /><br /><br />Alongside the powerful comparisons that I was able to draw between Power’s presentation of Atlantis’ hubris and our own, I also adored the characterization of Brigitte and D’vinid. Each has a strong soul, desiring peace and truth in a world gone mad. While Brigitte takes a more active approach and seems determined to help heal Atlantis, D’vinid takes a more individualised approach by playing soul-inspiring music to his fellow Atlanteans that are desperate for hope in times of crisis and great uncertainty.<br /><br /><br />The tension builds in each scene and had me clicking the pages of the ebook, intrigued to see what happened next. These moments were occasionally punctuated by lighthearted comedy and funnily enough, I found myself feeling less stressed by the potential consequences for our two heroes.<br /><br /><br />Overall, there’s an awful lot that could be said about this debut novel, too much for me to get down on paper or indeed online. If you're interested in ancient legends, lost civilisations, and in stories discussing what it truly means to be human in the face of adversity, then I’d recommended you Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening.<br /><br />My rating for this gripping and insightful read?<br />5 stars, easy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2911515969085344371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1629850136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629850136" />
    <a title="Sadaf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923426-sadaf"><img alt="Sadaf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464964829p2/10923426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629850136?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sadaf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sadaf" href="/user/show/10923426-sadaf">Sadaf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27428436-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629850136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7832965288775785057">I was offered a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review<br/><br/>There are books that people love and recommend all the time and then there are books like these. Not many people know about them but once you give them a chance, they completely blow you away. I was blown away from the first sentence and I'm still floating around somewhere. Beware, this book will never let you put your feet on the ground. Once you are under its spell, you are going to remain there forever. This is not a book you w</span>
  <span id="freeText7832965288775785057" style="display:none">I was offered a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review<br /><br />There are books that people love and recommend all the time and then there are books like these. Not many people know about them but once you give them a chance, they completely blow you away. I was blown away from the first sentence and I'm still floating around somewhere. Beware, this book will never let you put your feet on the ground. Once you are under its spell, you are going to remain there forever. This is not a book you will ever forget and I guarantee it will make a special place in your heart for itself. <br /><br />Fantasy, mythology, philosophy, romance, tragedy, humor, horror, adventure, thrill... this book lacks nothing. We follow the lives of various characters as they are pushed together by the well meaning but eccentric Fates and the ever aware Watchers. Every character is special. Every character has depth and a well developed back story and personality. They are all important and I couldn't wait till I saw them again at some point in the story. I loved them and hated them and loved them all over again. They may seem simple but every character is complex and intriguing.<br /><br />The lyrical prophecies especially captured my heart. They were so beautiful and perfect. I absolutely loved them. I don't think I have ever read a fantasy with world building this good. This is an aspect I cannot compromise on and I was not disappointed even once. Atlantis is not a new concept and to do that so well and so uniquely. The author deserves special applause for that. In so many ways Atlantis was just like any other thriving city today but so different at the same time. The customs, beliefs and way of life kept forcing me to compare the world around me to it and see if it really was any different from the reality around me.<br /><br />There are characters who challenge traditions and ask the right questions even though they seem so wrong to those around them. The philosophical debates and conversations alone are enough to recommend this book. Even though we have the prophecies to help us guess what happens next, things are never what they seem and unexpected things happen all the time. The mystery element remains throughout the plot and I was so shocked to learn that I had reached the end already. Not fair.<br /><br />I don't know how to get over this book. I don't. I recommend this to anyone who wants to lose themselves in Atlantis and perhaps find themselves in the same world they left behind.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7832965288775785057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2630023452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2630023452" />
    <a title="Brie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12379397-brie"><img alt="Brie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541695345p2/12379397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2630023452?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

<div id="review_1730169145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730169145" />
    <a title="Erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56812116-erica"><img alt="Erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508905432p2/56812116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730169145?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica" href="/user/show/56812116-erica">Erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27428436-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730169145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18328584251235653467">I wanted to like this book more than I did. Early on I was frequently distracted by the bizarre 'technologies' that the people possessed and the explanations of histories/famous past Atlanteans that peppered the pages. A ways into the book these seem to settle down and one could read it more for the story, but there was still a lot of set-up in this book that made it difficult to enjoy the underlying tale. Overall it was okay but I'm not sure I'll read the second one. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2683464826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683464826" />
    <a title="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez"><img alt="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467911475p2/56536968.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683464826?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" href="/user/show/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez">Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez?shelf=randr">randr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683464826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12474961438293435924">(English review + Reseña en Español)<br/><br/>Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening, by Mara Powers (326 pages, published by Shadows of Atlantis LLC, 2018), is the first part of the Shadows of Atlantis series, and is a mythical fiction and fantasy novel located in the third era of the enigmatic kingdom of Atlantis. The author has dedicated the book to "the awakening of humanity".<br/><br/>D'Vinid, a professional musician and an expert hoverboard trickster from Poseidia, Atlantis, tries to break the ties that eagerly tie h</span>
  <span id="freeText12474961438293435924" style="display:none">(English review + Reseña en Español)<br /><br />Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening, by Mara Powers (326 pages, published by Shadows of Atlantis LLC, 2018), is the first part of the Shadows of Atlantis series, and is a mythical fiction and fantasy novel located in the third era of the enigmatic kingdom of Atlantis. The author has dedicated the book to "the awakening of humanity".<br /><br />D'Vinid, a professional musician and an expert hoverboard trickster from Poseidia, Atlantis, tries to break the ties that eagerly tie his life to the design of the Watchers and live by his own standards, in a world that apparently clouds reason with dreams. Brigitte, from the Dreamvale, escapes from a growing disaster, leaving everything behind for a goal that has been predefined from above. Their paths will cross and take them both to the center of Atlantis, where they will be part of a gigantic struggle between fate and freedom, between conscience and blind faith.<br /><br />Through a fantastic but extremely thorough and quite coherent reconstruction of the ancient world of Atlantis, Mara Powers manages to present in Awakening a detailed allegory of the individual, social, religious and political struggles of the human race, confronting belief and technology, dreams and reality, freedom and destiny, light and shadows. The myriad of characters that make up this work have been defined with precision and rigor, and the story has been woven with such skill that the plot organically expands like a torch that gradually illuminates an immense labyrinth right from its center.<br /><br />Even though Awakening does not deliver a conclusion, its reading has been greatly pleasing and the journey exciting. This book does not lack action, humor, fantasy, romance or intrigue, and the promises it has placed on the horizon are powerful enough to wish to continue reading the rest of the series. A highly recommended book.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening, de Mara Powers (326 páginas, publicada por Shadows of Atlantis LLC, 2018), es la primera parte de la serie Shadows of Atlantis, y se trata de una novela de ficción mítica y fantasía ubicada en la tercera era del enigmático reino de la Atlántida. La autora ha dedicado el libro a “el despertar de la humanidad”.<br /><br />D’Vinid, músico de profesión y experto en trucos con el hoverboard, de Poseidia, Atlántida, trata de romper los lazos que empeñosamente atan su vida al designio de los Observadores y vivir bajo sus propias normas, en un mundo que aparentemente nubla la razón con sueños. Brigitte, del Dreamvale, escapa de un desastre creciente, dejándolo todo atrás por una meta que ha sido predefinida desde lo alto. Sus caminos se cruzarán y los llevarán a ambos al centro de la Atlántida, donde formarán parte de una lucha gigantesca entre el destino y la libertad, entre la conciencia y la fe ciega.<br />Mediante una reconstrucción fantástica pero extremadamente minuciosa y bastante coherente del antiguo mundo de la Atlántida, Mara Powers consigue presentar en Awakening una alegoría detallada de las luchas individuales, sociales, religiosas y políticas de la raza humana, confrontando la creencia y la tecnología, los sueños y la realidad, la libertad y el destino, la luz y las sombras. La miríada de personajes que componen esta obra han sido definidos con precisión y rigor, y la historia ha sido tejida con tal maestría que la trama se expande orgánicamente como una antorcha que ilumina paulatinamente un inmenso laberinto desde su centro.<br /><br />Aún cuando Awakening no entrega una conclusión, su lectura ha sido grandemente grata y el trayecto emocionante. A este libro no le falta acción, humor, fantasía, romance ni intriga, y las promesas que ha colocado en el horizonte son suficientemente poderosas para desear seguir leyendo el resto de la serie. Un libro muy recomendable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12474961438293435924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2611217913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2611217913" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2611217913?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2611217913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15483077003651062836">‘Atlantis remains firmly embedded in our collective psyche.’<br/><br/>Author Mara Powers has spent almost 30 years exploring the labyrinth of ancient civilizations. Her decision to turn it all into a high concept, visionary fantasy series stems from her study of the esoteric depiction of Atlantis. With the other half of her research rooted in the secular, it was the best way to illustrate both aspects of this fascinating legend. Her work is the legacy of the legend. She regularly migrates between Los Ange</span>
  <span id="freeText15483077003651062836" style="display:none">‘Atlantis remains firmly embedded in our collective psyche.’<br /><br />Author Mara Powers has spent almost 30 years exploring the labyrinth of ancient civilizations. Her decision to turn it all into a high concept, visionary fantasy series stems from her study of the esoteric depiction of Atlantis. With the other half of her research rooted in the secular, it was the best way to illustrate both aspects of this fascinating legend. Her work is the legacy of the legend. She regularly migrates between Los Angeles and San Francisco, California, Northern Colorado, Washington, D.C., New York City, and Austin, Texas.<br /><br />Mara has obviously intensely studied the history of Atlantis - and for those for whom this is the initial impression of Atlantis, ‘Atlantis is a fictional island mentioned within an allegory on the hubris of nations in Plato's works Timaeus and Critias, where it represents the antagonist naval power that besieges "Ancient Athens", the pseudo-historic embodiment of Plato's ideal state in The Republic. Mara has shaped mythology and history and literary freedom and has created a book that is not only fascinating reading, but also a text gook of sorts. At the back of her book she generously offers a cast of characters defined, and an exceptional glossary of terms used in this approach to Atlantis. <br /><br />At book’s end Mara shares her experience with her obsession with Atlantis – ‘There are two ways to approach the study of Atlantis, one is through secular subjects which are often considered “alternative.” The other is through the dazzling world of the esoteric. I find the latter reads like a science fiction novel. In choosing fiction, I could use these fantastic stories, and I didn’t need to back them up with hard facts. I just had to read and be inspired. To that end, I could also weave in my wider research on metaphysics, sociology and philosophy, as well as story-craft, a sprinkling of Jungian Psychology, and Joseph Campbell’s heroes journey… Do I believe in these stories? The answer is irrelevant. Because even Plato’s account of the discussion between Socrates and Solon about Atlantis is said to be an allegory about the downfall of Utopia by its own progress. The wave that sank Atlantis into the ocean is perhaps a metaphor for the destruction of humanity by the poison of our own psyche. These are the shadows of Atlantis… There are many aspects of my life experience woven into these pages. Struggles with addiction, abusers and sexual assault serve as a lesson for those who may have the same problems. The madness is based on the time I spent living in downtown Los Angeles near skid row watching the homeless epidemic happen around me. It is also a vehicle to demonstrate my theories about evil being an actual disease based on separation from unity consciousness. Hover Tricksters are my ode to the time I lived in Venice Beach where the skateboarders have achieved a level of fame. The conclaves are based on my time in the rave world and the festival circuit. The royal courts are based on the Renaissance reenactment world, otherwise known as SCA.’<br /><br />A lot of background for this novel, but necessary to reap the wonder the novel offers.<br /><br />The plot is complex but well distilled here – ‘Enter the legacy of the legend... Brigitte has been chosen to renew the treaty between Atlantis and the ancient bloodline of Lemuria. As an emissary of nature, her betrothal would ensure the continued function of the Crystal Grid, the life source of the ten kingdoms of Atlantis. But as Brigitte prepares to leave from her home in the magical Dreamvale, her people are attacked by a storm of shadows. Now she is running for her life. Upon her arrival in the ruling city of Atlantis, she meets D’Vinid, a dejected musician who lives the quintessential Atlantean lifestyle of revelry, escapism and apathy. Under the eclipse of a sacred festival, they are swept into an attraction they cannot resist. Their union may protect humanity from its worst enemy - the shadows of Atlantis. But there is one problem, this man is not her betrothed. Brigitte soon discovers that the corruption of the Grid could very well be the Grid itself. Citizens have neglected to attend the rituals required to charge the crystals with their psychic emanations. Some have fallen prey to an epidemic called “the madness”, caused by shadowy parasites that feed off human suffering. But as nature always strives toward balance, the crystals have activated a genetic upgrade among the people. The youth have begun to express supernatural powers. Could it be that D’Vinid and Brigitte are meant to be leaders among the awakened? And if so, why does it seem impossible for them to be together?’<br /><br />Take time and read this novel slowly. It is rich in content and fascinating in presentation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15483077003651062836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3649479424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3649479424" />
    <a title="Jessica Reads It" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46739531-jessica-reads-it"><img alt="Jessica Reads It" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588206979p2/46739531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3649479424?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Reads It" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Reads It" href="/user/show/46739531-jessica-reads-it">Jessica Reads It</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46739531-jessica-reads-it?shelf=myths-and-legends">myths-and-legends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3649479424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3078244838809382982">A story of two lovers separated by space and time, but joined together by fate.<br/><br/>The premise of Atlantic was captivating- a mysterious evil plaguing communities in its quest to destroy the dream-seer realms. I loved the concept of the watchers, intervening when humanity is led astray, and the variety of paranormal throughout the story. <br/><br/>D'Vinid was a dreamer and free spirit, led by his music and his insatiable appetite for new experiences. Bridgette could not be more opposite, her sense of duty and</span>
  <span id="freeText3078244838809382982" style="display:none">A story of two lovers separated by space and time, but joined together by fate.<br /><br />The premise of Atlantic was captivating- a mysterious evil plaguing communities in its quest to destroy the dream-seer realms. I loved the concept of the watchers, intervening when humanity is led astray, and the variety of paranormal throughout the story. <br /><br />D'Vinid was a dreamer and free spirit, led by his music and his insatiable appetite for new experiences. Bridgette could not be more opposite, her sense of duty and honor in stark contrast to D'Vinid. As the main characters, they were clearly defined and written quite beautifully. <br /><br />One of my peeves with this book is the sheer volume of new characters being introduced throughout the story. This book had a LOT going on, and you have to really pay attention to the introduction of characters and their role within the plot or you could get lost pretty quickly. While I appreciate the plot within the plot, within the plot, and the need to ensure all pieces of the story are covered, keeping track of ten plus characters is pretty tricky as a reader. <br /><br />Another thing I could not fully grasp within the story that negatively detracted from my overall experiences was the concept of "free-will" and its associated repercussions and the "traps of identity". I would not presume to know the author's intent but it came across as anti-individualism and slightly cult-like. Seeking to embrace free will should not lead to the downfall of society. <br /><br />Despite my differing opinions, I enjoyed the premise of the book and would consider reading the sequel to see if the grey areas are covered. Thank you to NetGalley, SOA LLC and Mara Powers for providing me with this arc. All views and opinions expressed are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3078244838809382982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2640895457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2640895457" />
    <a title="Kickass Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72978914-kickass-reads"><img alt="Kickass Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528210641p2/72978914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2640895457?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kickass Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kickass Reads" href="/user/show/72978914-kickass-reads">Kickass Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2640895457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18119767196019714914">If you are a fan of fantasy fiction like I am, then you will definitely enjoy 'Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening' by Mara Powers. It provides a unique take on the story of the mythical city of Atlantis, whilst weaving in a powerful love story, and plenty of supernatural peril. The plot focuses on Brigette who must travel to Atlantis to meet her betrothed, which is essential to the continued functioning of the Crystal Grid – the source of life to ten kingdoms. When she arrives she meets a man and fi</span>
  <span id="freeText18119767196019714914" style="display:none">If you are a fan of fantasy fiction like I am, then you will definitely enjoy 'Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening' by Mara Powers. It provides a unique take on the story of the mythical city of Atlantis, whilst weaving in a powerful love story, and plenty of supernatural peril. The plot focuses on Brigette who must travel to Atlantis to meet her betrothed, which is essential to the continued functioning of the Crystal Grid – the source of life to ten kingdoms. When she arrives she meets a man and finds herself falling in love, but he is not her betrothed and forces seem set on keeping them apart. There are other threats to Crystal Grid, mysterious shadows that spread sickness through the people of Atlantis, throwing nature and the Crystals out of balance. Can Brigette find a way to be with the man she loves and save the Ten Kingdoms, or will her entire world crumble?<br /><br />The fantasy novel is mysterious., alluring and so engaging. It draws you in from the very first chapter and takes you on a fast-paced journey of discovery and danger, right up to its unpredictable conclusion. I thoroughly enjoyed the first in the 'Shadows of Atlantis' series and I am very much looking forward to reading the next book in the series. Well done Mara Powers.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18119767196019714914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9022805541416773280">I have a real interest in mythology after studying it in college, so I was definitely drawn to Shadows of Atlantis as the reviews stated that historical legend and fact was weaved into the plot. I had high hopes for the first in Mara Power's fantasy saga and I was not disappointed. The scenes were set beautifully with detailed descriptions – I could almost see the ancient city of Atlantis with my own eyes. Additionally, Power has created two protagonists – Brigette and D'Vinid' that you cannot h</span>
  <span id="freeText9022805541416773280" style="display:none">I have a real interest in mythology after studying it in college, so I was definitely drawn to Shadows of Atlantis as the reviews stated that historical legend and fact was weaved into the plot. I had high hopes for the first in Mara Power's fantasy saga and I was not disappointed. The scenes were set beautifully with detailed descriptions – I could almost see the ancient city of Atlantis with my own eyes. Additionally, Power has created two protagonists – Brigette and D'Vinid' that you cannot help but become deeply invested in. The attraction between then is so powerful, but Brigette has been promised to another, to renew the bond between two Kingdom and strengthen the life force that sustains them all. However, there are shadows lurking in Atlantis that threaten the destroy everything – is this the end of the magical city.<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618482927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2206859076220890212">I really enjoyed this book. I haven't read fantasy or sci-fi in a long time. Atlantis is a marvelously complex and detailed world. I wish that more of the history of Atlantis was given because I felt lost at times. I also want to know more about the Watchers. There is a lot of room for a prequel if the author desires. There are many interesting characters that I hope will be developed further in later books. This series has a lot of potential.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2629374157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629374157" />
    <a title="Better Than Life" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90444804-better-than-life"><img alt="Better Than Life" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2629374157?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Better Than Life" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Better Than Life" href="/user/show/90444804-better-than-life">Better Than Life</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629374157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer77223170606936245">What a great first novel! Powers clearly is passionate about Atlantis, and does a great job creating and building a world for us to roam in. The world is very well-developed, along with the characters. The history and culture in the book is enough to draw us in, but Powers manages to drag us in deeper with skillful writing and bits of real history. It’s enough to have made me forget that I was reading a book, and felt a part of her universe. It’s hard to really focus on anything other the amazin</span>
  <span id="freeText77223170606936245" style="display:none">What a great first novel! Powers clearly is passionate about Atlantis, and does a great job creating and building a world for us to roam in. The world is very well-developed, along with the characters. The history and culture in the book is enough to draw us in, but Powers manages to drag us in deeper with skillful writing and bits of real history. It’s enough to have made me forget that I was reading a book, and felt a part of her universe. It’s hard to really focus on anything other the amazing attention to detail in the world/character building, as you might find from other reviews, but there’s a great story wrapped amidst it all as well. We get thrown into an adventure that is somewhat politically charged, but that fire is stoked by adventure, danger, and sacrifice. Brigitte is a solid character with diverse issues that really bring her to life in this story. If you haven’t already, give this book a shot. You wont be disappointed.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="77223170606936245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1265488030359459545" style="display:none">Mara Powers invites you to step into a fantastical and timeless world of dreams in this tightly-written journey, accompanied by great illustrations. <br /> <br />If you are intrigued by the sound of magical lands, parasitic shadows, tattoos that come to life, murder, elixirs, crystals, and apparitions made of fear then get lost in these pages as soon as you can! <br /> <br />The essence of the story is that the main character, Brigitte, and her brother, Lukias, journey to fulfil Brigitte’s birthright, to become the Queen of Atlantis. They must learn all about their new kingdom and its problems. <br /> <br />Without giving too much away, newly-betrothed Brigitte becomes pregnant, which of course is perfectly poised as material for Powers’s follow-up book to cover. Who is the father of her yet-to-be-born child though? Her new husband, King Kyliron or her lover, D’Vinid? </span>

<div id="review_2623214178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2623214178" />
    <a title="Valery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013735-valery"><img alt="Valery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480691033p2/4013735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2623214178?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valery" href="/user/show/4013735-valery">Valery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2623214178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3901512658941681525">Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening by Mara Powers takes this legend into new and different territory. It appears that the author has researched the legend of Atlantis extensively,and this shows in the writing. This book is full of the metaphysical, new inventions and technology, and fantasy, all captured in this epic tale. With a wonderfully put together story that plays off of history, as well as mythological history, the author has done her research. Great characters, along with a compelling story</span>
  <span id="freeText3901512658941681525" style="display:none">Shadows of Atlantis: Awakening by Mara Powers takes this legend into new and different territory. It appears that the author has researched the legend of Atlantis extensively,and this shows in the writing. This book is full of the metaphysical, new inventions and technology, and fantasy, all captured in this epic tale. With a wonderfully put together story that plays off of history, as well as mythological history, the author has done her research. Great characters, along with a compelling story line keep this from becoming a rather dry tome, while a complex plot keeps your interest as you learn of this unusual world. Highly recommend for something a little different, magical places and events, and an often light and fascinating writing style. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3901512658941681525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2667351839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2667351839" />
    <a title="Biblio Phanatic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74432236-biblio-phanatic"><img alt="Biblio Phanatic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2667351839?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Biblio Phanatic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Biblio Phanatic" href="/user/show/74432236-biblio-phanatic">Biblio Phanatic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667351839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10212261394751331106">This great and imaginative book from author Mara Powers will totally draw you in to its world of wonders and mythical elements with the heroine being Brigitte and her brother Lukias as they are taken by some group called the Watchers to Atlantis (yes, Aquaman anyone, haha) to search for the one who will establish an alliance or something like that between their two worlds. Brigitte finds herself drawn to a mysterious man-creature by the name of D’vinid who seem to also eye her for his own intere</span>
  <span id="freeText10212261394751331106" style="display:none">This great and imaginative book from author Mara Powers will totally draw you in to its world of wonders and mythical elements with the heroine being Brigitte and her brother Lukias as they are taken by some group called the Watchers to Atlantis (yes, Aquaman anyone, haha) to search for the one who will establish an alliance or something like that between their two worlds. Brigitte finds herself drawn to a mysterious man-creature by the name of D’vinid who seem to also eye her for his own interests. I was very taken in by the book’s simple writing and how fantastical it all is with the inhabitants of this version of Atlantis, the great and remarkable civilization of history and myth that many in our day talk about with awe and wonder.<br />I found this book to be very entertaining, romantic, adventurous and amazing. If you ever are in the loop for a book that takes place in Atlantis and is a lover of a fresh outlook about it then check this book out. The imagery is just fresh because everything about this Atlantis is drawn from Powers’ innovative and storytelling mind. There are creatures here that are called the Magi (hmmm…sounds familiar right?) Then there are characters with attire that will remind you of the characters of old fantasy mediums like hoods, scarves and crystals and stuff like that. There are the usual creatures of the sea like the dolphin for instance and then there is the inclusion of the Biblical hybrid we know as the Nephilim. All in all, if you are one who enjoys Sci-Fi/ Fantasy/ Bible/ and the great Ocean deep, this book is definitely for you. I know because I loved it after completing it! I won’t spoil the book for you so no more previews!<br />For these last few days of 2018, you should buy and read this ebook now! After your spiked interest in Atlantis maybe from viewing the Aquaman movie that’s out now this year (2018) this book I believe will sate you. Have a wonderful remainder of the old year and why not say goodbye to it with an amazing book like this?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10212261394751331106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1695345486" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1695345486" />
    <a title="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/800513-sarah-jayne-briggs"><img alt="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519179630p2/800513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695345486?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah-Jayne Briggs" href="/user/show/800513-sarah-jayne-briggs">Sarah-Jayne Briggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27428436-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695345486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9352437589165125586">(I received a free copy of this book in exchange for a review).<br/><br/>(This review may contain spoilers).<br/><br/>This was another book I really liked the sound of, but felt didn't live up to my expectations as I read it.<br/><br/>I wasn't quite sure what the main plot of the story was. I felt there was too much going on that wasn't drawn to a conclusion and that there were too many secondary characters and side plots.<br/><br/>I really liked being able to see the different types of technology on the island and it was also intrigu</span>
  <span id="freeText9352437589165125586" style="display:none">(I received a free copy of this book in exchange for a review).<br /><br />(This review may contain spoilers).<br /><br />This was another book I really liked the sound of, but felt didn't live up to my expectations as I read it.<br /><br />I wasn't quite sure what the main plot of the story was. I felt there was too much going on that wasn't drawn to a conclusion and that there were too many secondary characters and side plots.<br /><br />I really liked being able to see the different types of technology on the island and it was also intriguing to see something of their beliefs, even though I wasn't sure what was myth and what was true, or even really what sort of time period the book was set in.<br /><br />I would have liked some more details of how the madness worked, as there was very little detail about what caused it and why people who knew the sufferers wouldn't recognise them.<br /><br />I thought the hints of background between Belial and Kama were interesting and that was one of the few things I didn't have any problem understanding, even though I really didn't like the insta!love connection that formed.<br /><br />I thought there was a bit too much in the way of information dumping and I would have liked to see D'vinid's relationships with many of the other characters, such as the princes and Pan's twin sons. I would have liked to see many of the minor characters explored a bit more.<br /><br />It would have been good to see a bit more in the way of politics and how things had changed in the previous king's rule.<br /><br />I liked the use of the songs/poems in the book, though I would have liked to see more of how they fit in with D'vinid's title. I also found it very difficult to understand why he had so much trouble with the King... and it took a long time before I got any answers.<br /><br />I would have liked to see this book expanded upon a bit more and less characters to try and connect with. There was a lot that had potential here, but I did struggle to connect emotionally with the characters or really get to know what the culture was like. I'm not sure I would read the next book/s in this series, at least not unless it was a bit more focused on less characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9352437589165125586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1608388615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608388615" />
    <a title="Andy Peloquin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25866185-andy-peloquin"><img alt="Andy Peloquin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442969673p2/25866185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608388615?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Peloquin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Peloquin" href="/user/show/25866185-andy-peloquin">Andy Peloquin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27428436-shadows-of-atlantis">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608388615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2284348083310042775">I LOVED this version of Atlantis. It's definitely a very high fantasy concept, with its futuristic technology that goes far beyond basic medieval devices. The "hoverboard-like" devices in this story immediately brought to mind Back to the Future, but with a touch of Tony Hawk thrown in. A whole lot of fun!<br/><br/>The character of D'Vinid was well-written, as were most of the supporting characters. I found Brigitte to be just a tad too "feminine" (the clichéd femininity, rather than a real human woman) f</span>
  <span id="freeText2284348083310042775" style="display:none">I LOVED this version of Atlantis. It's definitely a very high fantasy concept, with its futuristic technology that goes far beyond basic medieval devices. The "hoverboard-like" devices in this story immediately brought to mind Back to the Future, but with a touch of Tony Hawk thrown in. A whole lot of fun!<br /><br />The character of D'Vinid was well-written, as were most of the supporting characters. I found Brigitte to be just a tad too "feminine" (the clichéd femininity, rather than a real human woman) for my tastes. While she never actually simpered or fluttered her eyelashes, it came close. I also HATED the "lovers destined to be reunited despite forbidden love" concept, but that's just me. I tend to take a much more pragmatic view toward romance and love.<br /><br />The world in which the story is set was highly detailed and vivid, and I could see most of Atlantis in my mind's eye as I read. Well done to the author for painting a graphic picture of this fantastical world.<br /><br />There were a lot of complex elements, some of which bordered on over-complicated. The "grids" and "crystals" were interesting, but there was a lot of over-explaining of some elements and not enough detail on others. I had to drop a star mainly because of this.<br /><br />The book's ending had no climax to it. I was waiting for a big build-up and dramatic scene at the end, but it just sort of slipped into the end with more of a whimper than a bang.<br /><br />However, all in all, the book was a work of art, one definitely worth reading! If you want a fresh take on the Atlantis myth, this is a solid choice.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2284348083310042775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2734843543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2734843543" />
    <a title="Jessica Bronder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5781282-jessica-bronder"><img alt="Jessica Bronder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310427273p2/5781282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734843543?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Bronder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Bronder" href="/user/show/5781282-jessica-bronder">Jessica Bronder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734843543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18226671041430103882">Atlantis is an amazing world that runs of the power of the Crystal Grid and the psychic power of the people. But the grid is failing. Bridgette is supposed to be the solution to fixing the problem. Brigette is to be married and the unity strengthens the grid. But when she gets to the center of Atlantis she meets D’Vinis, a musician with his own problems. <br/><br/>Brigette starts to fall for D’Vinis but he is not the one that she is supposed to be marrying. But this might just be what Atlantis needs. The </span>
  <span id="freeText18226671041430103882" style="display:none">Atlantis is an amazing world that runs of the power of the Crystal Grid and the psychic power of the people. But the grid is failing. Bridgette is supposed to be the solution to fixing the problem. Brigette is to be married and the unity strengthens the grid. But when she gets to the center of Atlantis she meets D’Vinis, a musician with his own problems. <br /><br />Brigette starts to fall for D’Vinis but he is not the one that she is supposed to be marrying. But this might just be what Atlantis needs. The grid is the problem and the people not coming to the rituals to renew it are not helping keep it going. But it seems the younger generation has developed some abilities that just might change the way things work.<br /><br />This was an interesting read. I love the idea of Atlantis so I was jumping at the chance to review this book. I loved this world and how it worked, although it was a bit of a learning curve when I started reading the book. But once I got things figured out it was easy to follow along with the different characters.<br /><br />This story has so much more than just Brigette and D’Vinis. You have political issues, religious issues, and changes with people and society. It does make you think. I really enjoyed this book and recommend you check it out. It is a great start to a series with lots of possibilities. I can’t wait to see where Mara Powers takes the story from here.<br /><br />I received a complimentary copy of this book. I voluntarily chose to read and post an honest review.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10298230306472511279">I received a copy as a Goodreads giveaway.<br/><br/>The story revolves around D'Vinid, a self-absorbed, broody individual, who thinks just like all self-absorbed, broody individuals, that his problems are worse than anyone else's problems. If this was the whole story, I would have stopped reading it by page 20.   <span id="freeText10298230306472511279" style="display:none">I received a copy as a Goodreads giveaway.<br /><br />The story revolves around D'Vinid, a self-absorbed, broody individual, who thinks just like all self-absorbed, broody individuals, that his problems are worse than anyone else's problems. If this was the whole story, I would have stopped reading it by page 20. But to have this person placed in the setting of Atlantis, a land that the author wisely chooses not to be as idyllic as the descriptions of Plato, creates for an interesting tale. And after meeting with Brigitte (who is destined to be Queen of Atlantis), he finds that the fates have given him a much larger role in the future of Atlantis than one of his stature should expect to play.<br /><br />The storyline moves the reader along except for the annoying short foreshadowing scenes that are endemic to multiple part book series. I was interested in the book based on my previous reading on the myths and conjectures on Atlantis, but is a book for all genre readers. For those without the Atlantis background, the author includes a glossary of terms which includes all of the key figures in the story.</span>

<div id="review_3156638460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Anya Pavelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79829955-anya-pavelle"><img alt="Anya Pavelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569768351p2/79829955.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>
